O you, very dear sons, I have finished this book which is the end of the science of medicine, assembled from its teachings and pronouncements. And it came to pass that I realized I must accompany this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, namely surgery.</start_of_turn>
And because the work of hands is fraught in our region and is strange to all, if the science is lost and forgotten, and nothing remains of it except for the small descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have performed.</start_of_turn And from this arises the error and the emptiness, and are closed the understandings and is displaced the science.</start_of_turn
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.
Or it seems to me that I shall make it live altogether the order of this physician according to the way of exposure and declaration and of the abbreviation; and I shall join together the forms of the instruments of cautery, and of other instruments of the work with the arrangement of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary.</start_of_turn> And it is necessary that he who enters this field should be skilled in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he has grasped the judgment of limbs, and the forms and the joints and the separations of things, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles and their number, and the structure and the veins moving and resting, and their issue.</start_of_turn>
And thus Hippocrates teaches us that with the hand one must not touch, but must work with the work; and in the art of healing.
We are told in the beginning of this book that he who is not skilled in the things that are before him, if he dares to handle them without caution and respect, will often cause more harm than good; as I have often seen happen in this science, when people abandon both science and sense.
For I have seen a madman who, when he has incised a scrophule or the neck of a woman, has also cut the arteries of the neck; and so much blood has flowed out that the woman has died between his hands.
And thus another marvel which treats a stone of a bladder stone, and the stone was large; if it took away with it a piece of the bladder, and remained in the body for two days.
And thus I have already been called to treat it, and I saw the disposition of the patient and the greatness of the stone, and if it were cut out it would surely die.</start_of_turn>
And thus another marvel which treats a limb broken in our land which had a wound; and with the fracture it had a wound; and the physicians of this land were unable to rejoin the fracture above the wound as these things are often done by strong bands, and did not leave the wound open, and left it until it was finished; and they commanded that it should not be moved; and when the limb was whole again and the bone and the flesh were lost, it was finished.</start_of_turn>
I beseech thee to come hither, and I hasten to come and loosen the limb; and when I see it dislocated, there is peace and no pain is felt.
But every way the corruption is already confirmed or the limb is unsound, and it will not be healed; and the corruption will persist as long as the limb is completely lost
And thus another mire which undermines the bone marrow swells, and then inflames from the malice of its lordship.
For cancer, when it is pure of melancholy humor, does not yield except when iron is touched upon it unless all the corrupted parts can be removed.
And thus, know this well, that the work of hands has become divided into twelve divisions: that is to say, where there is peril in many things; and I shall show in every chapter of this book where there is doubt and peril.
For you must always bear this in mind, so that the fools may not speak badly of you.
If you take up arms in custody, and undertake your patients gently and steadily, and use the better way so that by the grace of God you may come out whole and sound; and leave the grievous diseases in their rightful place; and stay by your arms from that from which you may doubt, and hope that you may pass from this world to the next in glory.
The fires of punishment are like the thorns of suffering: “Do not take care of your ailments in this way, for only fools are called to such madness.”
I have devised this treatment according to two chapters
The first chapter concerns fire cautery and aqueous medicine, and the chapter orders from the head down; and about the forms of instruments, and instruments of cautery, and everything that is necessary for the work
The second chapter deals with cutting and piercing, and the dressing of wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapter orders and the forms of instruments.
The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered from the shoulder chief down to the feet, and from the forms of the instruments.
As we have remembered from the work, it is necessary to say the quality of the aid and the great discomfort of great complexion.
I say that the quality of the aid, and the discomfort, is the longest word and the most subtle science and the greatest secret; and about this many have spoken, and they agree on this; and I am suffocated by their words, because I reduce the length.
I say that the fire cautery helps universally for all complexion or there is matter, for it is to say complexion hot sense matter, and complexion dry sense matter.
In complexion chaude et seche, matters assemblement, they declare that the cautery is of great aid; and others declare the contrary: that the cautery is of no avail in disease but comes from heat and drought.
For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be the cure for hot diseases by heat, but by drought; and thus those who say the opposite that the cautery does great aid in hot and dry diseases that arise in the bodies of men.</start_of_turn> For when you compare the body of a man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body dry.</start_of_turn
And I consent to this word. For I have never seen it happen before in practice.</start_of_turn>
And thus, in no way do I know of anyone who has ever experienced such a thing except for those who have seen it, who know by long experience the chapter of cautery, the variety of complexion of men, and the causes and dispositions of their diseases, and the results and the causes of their pains; for other complexions we have no experience, even in cold and moist diseases.</start_of_turn And all the more must they agree to the cautery.
And know this, sir, that cautery with fire is more effective for secret cures than burning cautery.
For fire is simple, and brings no further heat than to the member that is being cauterized, and harms no other member save its name.</start_of_turn>
Burning medicines come from one member to another, causing grief and disease to the member; and by chance it harms the patient.</start_of_turn>
Fire, by its height and for the goodness of its substance, does not make this worse, if there is no excess.</start_of_turn
And this I have learned through experience and by the length of my service and study in this art, and it is confirmed by the truth of things; and for this reason I apologize for the length of my words, for it does not please me to keep silent the secret which is returned or the fire, and the quality of this work, as it unravels the diseases of the body, as the philosopher demonstrates; or you may follow this in your thoughts.
Know, son, that it is necessary to determine at what tension the cautery should be made, and when they are pricked.</start_of_turn>
I say that the cautery is useful in all tensions, for the harmful effects resulting from it are overcome by the aid of the cautery; and indeed if the cautery is for necessary pains that are urgent and cannot wait until the greater harm is removed from the limb.</start_of_turn
And think not, dear son, if the madman makes fools of himself; for the disease which is cured by cautery has no return; and he says so; but it is not thus if they are cured, for cauteries are but medicine which moves the complexion, and dries the humors which are the cause of the pain, and is worth more than medicine for its promptness of value, and for the excellence of its work and its sovereignty.
Indeed, it is known that disease does not arise at any time according to the complexion of the patient and the nature of the disease and its virtue; and there are assembled in him the superfluities by the acquisition of foods and similar things, except when cauteries are administered in place or if there is little superfluity and moisture, for as with cauteries of the dense kind for pain, and the similar things, and part of the pain does not return again; but this often happens.</start_of_turn>
And many people do not understand that cauteries are not called medicine, and that is true; but they do not believe that cauteries are worth more than medicine, but their understanding is false, for cauteries are the last of medicine for in no disease have we administered remedies that have not been useful, so we administer the cautery, and it is worth more.</start_of_turn> Therefore, even though cautery is behind medicine, it does not please the minds of fools.
The ancients say that golden cautery is more stupid than iron, and they say that fire only comes from the quality of gold and the height of its substance; and they say that the lead of the cautery does not cause harm, but this is not seen because I have proved it, and I have found that it is like in certain men; and golden cautery is worth as much as iron, as they say.</start_of_turn>
And indeed, whenever you burn an instrument of gold, you do not know how much it is scorched by the color of gold, and when it has cooled down; and if you burn it too much, there is fire; and there is enough hindrance.
And for this reason we use our fire cautery, as we have learned from experience.

olive cautery

from pores that come as pieces
Many times it happens that by a sudden discharge of humours a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a great and bloody matter. And the cautery of this disease is as follows. That is, cautery of fire and cautery of hot water. The cautery of fire is that you should grasp the hair as though it were a pin of wool, and make it of fine iron to the measure that it can penetrate the clot of all parts, and that there be subtle margins; after that put all around the clot, and hold your hand tightly around the clot until it comes to the front of the clot; and leave it thus for two days until it begins to soften by putrefaction; then make an embolus of wild mallow bruised with oil, and leave the embolus on all night, and close the wound carefully and remove the sutures from their roots. Then cure the wound by applying charcoal as long as it is sane.
And if they are converted by discharge of humours from the head and hands and in the feet, if you must do so, bring a cautery of hot water; and this is partly in manner: take a bowl of lead or iron, or a pin of wool, and put it on the clot and the underlay; that is, put nails on the edges. And put the bowl on so that it encloses everything, then put a little of warm oil on it, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand by turning so that the margin of the bowl comes to the root of the clot, and can find the hot water going deep down to the root; and offer the patient a little of the hot water an hour; then leave it thus, and it will drain out all at its roots. Thus do another, until you have removed all that is at the head, and then cure the wounds that have arisen from charcoal.

When the tooth is loose.
When the tooth is loose, whether by percussion or by biting, and the patient is unable to press upon it without it bleeding, you must cure it with restrictive medicines. This is of no avail; if you command it to be restrained with a golden thread, for the silver thread becomes green and corrupts, but the tooth does not move. Let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are aligned, take the thread and double it between the two front teeth, then put the teeth between the other teeth as many as there are, until you see it clearly up to the sound tooth on the other side; then finish the coverage up to the part where you began, and strain your hand steadily and cautiously, so that it does not move; or if you bind it to the root of the tooth if it cannot escape. And I treated a woman with a wound in her throat, which is to say, a wound of little size; and she could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and she could not eat or drink, and she died because she fainted from pain or from fear. The wound was so high that it had forced two nails through two holes that did not exist. I therefore did the following, and put one finger on the wound and held it tight, and then pushed out a great piece of bone; and then I closed the other part of the hole through which the nail had passed, and I closed the mouth and pressed the tongue; and then I put the finger back in the wound and closed a part of it, and only a little blood came out. And I removed the passage from the throat of the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and she did not stop fainting from that wound for a long time; and the wound healed again, and filled the space that I had evacuated, until it grew large; then I bound it and cauterized it in the throat: and that was the end of the matter.

From the navel.
This cure is more secure than incision, for it is cured by fumigation according to this method. Hermofrodie est selonc deux manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les deux coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et deux coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.
Hermaphroditism is in two ways like that of women: one if between the two testicles appears as in the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine.  And the other way if it is in women, and has on the navel like a beard and two testicles.  And the cure for the shame and the fame if it is that you cut off the testicles altogether, and the cure is like other wounds; in the second way, of those homes whose urine spurts through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene is a swelling above the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have it as much as a hand.  This is the cure. It is necessary to hold the excess of the swelling at your hand or armpit, and to press it lightly; and do not move too much, for bleeding will not come, then the cure will be like any other cure as long as it is healthy; and there is another disease that comes from the root of the maw, and the spleen, and by chance spurts out, and is like the semblance of a knot, and for this reason it is called the ancient “madness of the womb”. If you can cut it out, as we have said concerning the tenticle, and cure it as long as it is healthy.
De erratique.
When something is out of its usual or proper place.
From hemorrhoids.
Emorroids are openings of veins which without restraint usually occur; and when they are old, they become thickened. We have already mentioned in the division the signs and symptoms; and I will say here those which resolve the cure. I say that emorroids and thick blood, when they are mixed in the marrow, and are not perceptible to the touch, if not treated with iron. Those which are at the edge of the marrow, we can perceive, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then extend the ankle and grasp the heel, then sprinkle on medicinal astringents such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then remove the pieces an hour later, and put them in cold water; and if there is any bleeding, if you make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and saffron and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and assails, and make one plaster on her back. And if it is fainting, that is good. If this does not happen, if there is still bleeding at the edge, make a wound there with a needle; then take lint and moisten it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make the wound bleed. And when the wound has healed, if the bleeding has ceased, that which is called ‘albathir’ is red, and is similar to a rough chief, if you cover it as I have said the thickened blood; and then the bleeding will cease.

From infancy.
From infancy. A master first learns at play what is the natural figure of infancy, and the signs are when you see the woman press her belly and desire to smell the breast: then the child immediately sucks; and when the child’s limbs are in accordance with the natural figure, and his head comes out first, and the second comes with him; and when you see these signs, if you gently press his belly, if the child sucks, that is enough; for when he descends on his head, if the second comes with him, and the mother is contented with his superabundances by his good upbringing; this is not natural. For it never comes from his toes, but from the womb or the hips, or the hands, or from his belly, or from behind, and is caused by some chance or other evil figure; if the master is learned in play to be wise and discreet in these things, and is wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures in which you must help him.
When the child comes out of his head naturally, and the woman gives birth and her strength is weak, if you make her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and she gives birth of oil or fennel or whatever is pleasing, and then you must hold the child between her two legs, which is his natural shape: And split the second finger, and bind its nail until the moisture that is in its core comes out; and press the woman’s belly until the fetus descends, and if it does not descend, if you must, clench the woman with muscle spasm of ruegra with oil of sesame; then make her take and expel menstrual blood, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if the fetus is now expelled. And if the two hands go out forcefully, if you must, hold them lightly together and together; and if they will not enter, if put the woman on the seat, and hold her feet high; then pull the seat out of the ground, and hold her, that she does not move during the pulling; and if the hands do not enter, and the fetus dies, if you grip the hands at the wrist that was put before, and pull out the child, and comfort her equally.

From the dislocation of the shoulder
And there are two ways to reset the dislocation: one is to take a fist full of moist earth and form it into a cone-shape; then put the limb over the fist, as far up as the armpit, and hold it there with the fist under the armpit; then put the hand over the break without any weight or support from the attendants; then put the patient’s hands together, so that the break returns naturally.

Of the fracture of bones due to violence.
At the ankle, fracture does not arise; but in bones of violence, fracture never comes alone, and there must be two together; and there is no other cause of death but certainty and fear.
And if there is a fracture in bones of violence, and you see these bones pushing against each other, if you put the limb so sick on the earth, as if it were falling from the sky, and then put your limb on the ground, where the bones are raised, then press the limb until it returns to its place; then put on the dressing and bandage, and put some small weights on the belly of the limb, and hold the limb firmly, and as soon as the limb has healed, wrap it in bandages, and other things that you must provide.

Hair that comes out with the scab
Hair that comes out with the scab comes out many times after the heat of the wound, even when it is close to the joint, and is a helpful sign that the limb is recovering naturally.
Take care then that it is fresh: if you give astringents such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acacia, and similar things, that you do not take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with a strong wine or with eggs or with oil; and put them on the wound in bandages, and strain it well, and do not remove it from the hand for days; and then remove it, and start another one, until the nodulation is bony; or you strain it on a well-made piece of leather; for the property of leather is that it will harden all the swellings under the limb; and if the nodulation has already turned into hardness just like stone, and it is necessary to harden it, if the swelling above is complete, and remove the excess; or do not remove it at all, until it is bony, and cure it until it is healed.
When the bone is restored and the limb is weak and limp, if there is any discomfort: sometimes because it was too tightly bound and was not loosened enough; or because there are too many bands, and it cannot move smoothly; or from too many wounds; or from excessive movements, not in its proper place; or because there is too much blood in the limb, if it is weak.
And the cure is to make the patient walk and keep the limb firm, until it is multiplied in him; and give him baths, and make him cheerful and comfortable; then put a poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to great nourishment, and the wound often bleeds profusely until the nourishment comes to the limb; and bring it back to its natural shape.

And so begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
When dislocation comes to no more, if you can now restore the limb to its proper position.
For if it is late, if it has swollen already, and by chance if one attempts to reset it, there will be prickings at the root; for because of this one must not move it while it is swollen: many times it has brought on vomiting and other pains.
When this has happened, if the patient is still able to move, let the patient rest; once the swelling has subsided, warm and oil the limb, then gently restore it to its place. Cure each limb individually as needed.
And I have ordered the chapters concerning dislocations of the shoulder joint to the end.

Of the dislocation of the shoulder.
The shoulder is dislocated only by two means: firstly, that it be dislocated at the armpit downwards; and secondly, that it be dislocated at the shoulder-blade downwards; and sometimes at the top of the shoulder-blade, and this is dangerous.
It does not come loose behind for the shoulder, and does not come loose from the nerves; and many times it comes loose downwards towards the armpit, even among those who have little flesh, for at these jumps there is great pain; among those who have enough flesh, there are jumps with pain, and they return with pain.
And sometimes there are percussion or fractures, and the shoulder is inflamed by a thick abscess, and care must be taken that it is not dislocated by this.
It is necessary that you be certain that it is actually dislocated; and once you are sure, then you may begin treatment.
Dislocation is known when the shoulder is displaced toward the back, and the difference between the affected and healthy shoulder will be evident; you will find between them a noticeable separation and at the top of the shoulder you will find a socket, and when the shoulder is pressed against the socket, just as if it were a bone; and the patient is unable to raise their arm to its original position, or to move in any way
and thus too, if it is dislocated upwards, if not hidden, because you will see it immediately;
And this manner of dislocation is not without force to restore it, when it is new, or when the limb is painful.
And the way is to take hold of the painful limb with the hand above, then put your thumbs under the armpit, and take hold of the joint forcefully upwards; and then the hand must be held and stretched upwards, because it must be set in place.</start_of_turn>
And if it does not come as we have said above, if it is to be believed that the patient is to be bathed in warm water; and it is to be given soothing and comforting nourishment, such as a decoction of elderberry and fennel and honey in water, and to be given.</start_of_turn
Then either keep the patient still on his back, and put under the armpit a cushion of linen equal in size, not too soft nor too hard, and put the hand of the shoulder over the cushion, and keep the shoulder joint firmly in place, and treat the painful hand.</start_of_turn
And another attendant holds the patient’s head still, so that it does not move downwards; for the shoulder joint returns immediately, and if you see that it remains fixed in this manner, you must rejoin it in this way.

And another attendant grasps the patient’s hand downwards towards the belly. And if the patient is too light, if you put anything heavy with him, the dislocation will return immediately.

Dislocations of the shoulder
Dislocations of the shoulder are only caused by dislocations of the shoulder and elbow joints; they do not occur with other joints. The dislocation of the shoulder is impaired in three parts: front and back, and above and below; the greater the displacement in front and back, the greater the impairment.
